<p><b>Dries Mertens</b> (<small>Dutch pronunciation:&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[dris mrtns]</a></span>, born 6 May 1987), nicknamed Ciro,<sup id="cite_ref-nieuwsblad1_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nieuwsblad1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nieuwsblad_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nieuwsblad-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> is a Belgian professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Striker" title="Forward (association football)">striker</a> or <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Winger" title="Midfielder">winger</a> for Italian club <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium national team</a>. Mertens is Napoli's all time top goalscorer.<sup id="cite_ref-nieuwsblad1_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nieuwsblad1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nieuwsblad_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nieuwsblad-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a youth, Mertens played for <a href="/wiki/K._Stade_Leuven" title="K. Stade Leuven">Stade Leuven</a>, <a href="/wiki/R.S.C._Anderlecht" title="R.S.C. Anderlecht">Anderlecht</a> and <a href="/wiki/K.A.A._Gent" title="K.A.A. Gent">Gent</a>, and made his debut on loan to <a href="/wiki/SC_Eendracht_Aalst" class="mw-redirect" title="SC Eendracht Aalst">Eendracht Aalst</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Third_Division" title="Belgian Third Division">Belgian Third Division</a>. In 2006, he moved to Dutch <a href="/wiki/Eerste_Divisie" title="Eerste Divisie">Eerste Divisie</a> club <a href="/wiki/AGOVV_Apeldoorn" class="mw-redirect" title="AGOVV Apeldoorn">AGOVV Apeldoorn</a>, where he spent three years before a €600,000 move to <a href="/wiki/FC_Utrecht" title="FC Utrecht">Utrecht</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Eredivisie" title="Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a>. Two years later he and teammate <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Strootman" title="Kevin Strootman">Kevin Strootman</a> were transferred to <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV Eindhoven</a> for a combined fee of €13 million, and won the <a href="/wiki/KNVB_Cup" title="KNVB Cup">KNVB Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff_Shield" title="Johan Cruyff Shield">Johan Cruyff Shield</a> in 2012. In 2013, Mertens signed for Napoli for a €9.6 million fee and has since made over 300 appearances for the club. He won the <a href="/wiki/Coppa_Italia" title="Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Supercoppa_Italiana" title="Supercoppa Italiana">Supercoppa Italiana</a> in 2014, and was named in the <a href="/wiki/Serie_A_Team_of_the_Year" title="Serie A Team of the Year">Serie A Team of the Year</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Serie_A" title="2016–17 Serie A">2016–17</a> season. In 2020, he scored his 122nd goal for the club, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Marek_Ham%C5%A1%C3%ADk" title="Marek Hamšík">Marek Hamšík</a> as Napoli's <a href="/wiki/List_of_S.S.C._Napoli_records_and_statistics#Top_goalscorers" title="List of S.S.C. Napoli records and statistics">all-time top goalscorer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mertens made his Belgium debut in 2011 and has since made over 90 appearances for the national team. He was also part of the nation's squads at the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>, helping them to a third-place finish at the latter tournament. In 2016, he was named Belgian Footballer of the Year.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dries_Mertens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dries_Mertens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Leuven" title="Leuven">Leuven</a>, Belgium, Mertens started his career as a boy at the now-dissolved local club <a href="/wiki/K._Stade_Leuven" title="K. Stade Leuven">Stade Leuven</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> It was here that the scouts of <a href="/wiki/R.S.C._Anderlecht" title="R.S.C. Anderlecht">Anderlecht</a> first spotted Mertens, ultimately resulting in him being offered a chance to join the club's youth academy in 1998. He spent five years in the youth setup at Anderlecht before being released in 2003, with coaches finding him to be too be too short and physically incapable of competing at a professional level.<sup id="cite_ref-start_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-start-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Following his release from Anderlecht, Mertens was signed by fellow <a href="/wiki/Belgian_First_Division_A" title="Belgian First Division A">Belgian Pro League</a> side, <a href="/wiki/K.A.A._Gent" title="K.A.A. Gent">Gent</a>. Following two seasons in Gent's youth academy, Mertens was <a href="/wiki/Loan_(sports)" title="Loan (sports)">loaned</a> to <a href="/wiki/S.C._Eendracht_Aalst" title="S.C. Eendracht Aalst">Eendracht Aalst</a> for the 2005–06 season. He excelled with the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Third_Division" title="Belgian Third Division">third division</a> side and was named Player of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-start_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-start-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The coaching staff at Gent, much like those at Anderlecht before, remained unconvinced of Mertens given his slight frame, however, and loaned him out again the following season, this time to <a href="/wiki/AGOVV_Apeldoorn" class="mw-redirect" title="AGOVV Apeldoorn">AGOVV Apeldoorn</a> in the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-start_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-start-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="AGOVV">AGOVV</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dries_Mertens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: AGOVV">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 1 July 2006, Mertens officially signed for AGOVV Apeldoorn, who later dissolved in 2013, on a season-long loan with the option of purchase.<sup id="cite_ref-start_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-start-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> He managed a return of 2 goals in 35 appearances during a season which saw him become a fan favourite amongst <i>De Blauwen</i> supporters. Mertens' form prompted AGOVV, led by new <a href="/wiki/Manager_(association_football)" title="Manager (association football)">manager</a> <a href="/wiki/John_van_den_Brom" title="John van den Brom">John van den Brom</a>, to exercise the option to sign the Belgian permanently the following season. It was a move that paid off for the Dutch club as Mertens ended the season having 15 goals in 38 appearances for the club.<sup id="cite_ref-start_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-start-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Such was his influence that Mertens was named new club captain for the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Eerste_Divisie" title="2008–09 Eerste Divisie">2008–09 Eerste Divisie</a> season.<sup id="cite_ref-f442_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-f442-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Mertens excelled in his new role and contributed a further 13 goals for the season which contributed to him being awarded the Golden Bull award for the most talented player in the <a href="/wiki/Eerste_Divisie" title="Eerste Divisie">Eerste Divisie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ed_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ed-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> It would be his last season with the club, however, as at the end of the season he agreed to join <a href="/wiki/Eredivisie" title="Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a> side <a href="/wiki/FC_Utrecht" title="FC Utrecht">Utrecht</a>. Mertens made 110 appearances across all competitions for AGOVV during his three seasons at the club and netted 31 goals.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dries_Mertens_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Dries_Mertens_2.jpg/170px-Dries_Mertens_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="304" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b4/Dries_Mertens_2.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="229" data-file-height="410" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dries_Mertens_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mertens training with <a href="/wiki/FC_Utrecht" title="FC Utrecht">Utrecht</a> in 2009.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Utrecht">Utrecht</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dries_Mertens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Utrecht">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Having agreed a deal with AGOVV in March 2009, Utrecht officially completed the signing of Mertens at the start of the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Eredivisie" title="2009–10 Eredivisie">2009–10 Eredivisie</a> season for a <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a>600,000 <a href="/wiki/Transfer_(association_football)" title="Transfer (association football)">transfer</a> fee.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In his debut season with the club, Mertens netted six league goals en route to being named runner-up to <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Luis_Su%C3%A1rez" title="Luis Suárez">Luis Suárez</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="Dutch Footballer of the Year">Dutch Footballer of the Year</a> award. He was also awarded the <a href="/wiki/David_di_Tommaso#Di_Tommaso_Trophy" class="mw-redirect" title="David di Tommaso">Di Tommaso Trophy</a> for Utrecht's Player of the Season.<sup id="cite_ref-start_10-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-start-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He improved on his tally the following season, netting 10 goals in 31 league appearances for Utrecht, including a final day <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> against <a href="/wiki/AZ_Alkmaar" title="AZ Alkmaar">AZ</a>, and a further three goals in his first experience in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In total, Mertens scored 14 goals across all competitions and contributed 24 assists.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> It proved to be his last season at the club, though, as his form at the <a href="/wiki/Stadion_Galgenwaard" title="Stadion Galgenwaard">Stadion Galgenwaard</a> caught the attention of some of the league's biggest clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-start_10-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-start-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Mertens' two-season spell in Utrecht yielded 21 goals in 86 appearances across all competitions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="PSV_Eindhoven">PSV Eindhoven</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dries_Mertens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: PSV Eindhoven">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In June 2011, it was announced that Mertens had signed for fellow Eredivisie club <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV Eindhoven</a> as a replacement for the departing <a href="/wiki/Bal%C3%A1zs_Dzsudzs%C3%A1k" title="Balázs Dzsudzsák">Balázs Dzsudzsák</a> in a dual transfer with Utrecht teammate <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Strootman" title="Kevin Strootman">Kevin Strootman</a> for a combined fee of €13&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> He scored on his competitive debut for the club on 7 August 2011, netting PSV's only goal in a 3–1 loss to AZ.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, on 28 August, Mertens scored his first hat-trick for PSV in a 6–1 drubbing of <a href="/wiki/S.B.V._Excelsior" class="mw-redirect" title="S.B.V. Excelsior">Excelsior</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Mertens' strong start to season culminated with him netting four goals in a 7–1 rout of <a href="/wiki/Roda_JC_Kerkrade" title="Roda JC Kerkrade">Roda JC</a> on 24 September 2011, meaning he had scored 11 goals in his first 7 appearances for PSV.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Towards the back end of the campaign, Mertens lost a number of teeth during a collision with <a href="/wiki/Heracles_Almelo" title="Heracles Almelo">Heracles</a> goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Remko_Pasveer" title="Remko Pasveer">Remko Pasveer</a>, although he managed to score during the incident. It was revealed on social media platform <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> that Pasveer had found one of Mertens' teeth lodged in his head three weeks after the players had collided.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Mertens ultimately ended the season having scored 21 goals in 33 matches, the fourth highest in the Eredivisie. He also scored three goals in four <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_KNVB_Cup" title="2011–12 KNVB Cup">KNVB Cup</a> matches, including a header in the final at <a href="/wiki/De_Kuip" title="De Kuip">De Kuip</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>, leading PSV to a 3–0 win over Heracles.<sup id="cite_ref-KNVB_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KNVB-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mertens_PSV_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Mertens_PSV_2012.jpg/170px-Mertens_PSV_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Mertens_PSV_2012.jpg/255px-Mertens_PSV_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/Mertens_PSV_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="272" data-file-height="382" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mertens_PSV_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mertens played for Dutch side <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV Eindhoven</a> between 2011 and 2013.</div></div></div>
<p>Mertens added to his silverware at the start of the following season as PSV beat Ajax 4–2 to lift the <a href="/wiki/2012_Johan_Cruyff_Shield" title="2012 Johan Cruyff Shield">Johan Cruyff Shield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JCS_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JCS-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> On 30 September 2012, Mertens and <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Locadia" title="Jürgen Locadia">Jürgen Locadia</a>, who was making his Eredivisie debut, both scored hat-tricks as PSV defeated <a href="/wiki/VVV-Venlo" title="VVV-Venlo">VVV-Venlo</a> 6–0.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Mertens ultimately scored 14 league goals, and 16 across all competitions as PSV ended the season as runners-up to Ajax in the Eredivisie. He also aided his side's cause with a further 17 assists.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> It would be his final season in the Eredivisie, however, as at the conclusion of the campaign PSV accepted an offer from <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> side <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a> for his signature.<sup id="cite_ref-PN_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PN-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Mertens departed Eindhoven having made 88 appearances and scored 45 goals over the course of two seasons.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Napoli">Napoli</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dries_Mertens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Napoli">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mertens' agent <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B8ren_Lerby" title="Søren Lerby">Søren Lerby</a> confirmed on 16 June 2013 that the player had agreed to sign with <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a>. He became <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez" title="Rafael Benítez">Rafael Benítez</a>'s first signing as new Napoli <a href="/wiki/Manager_(association_football)" title="Manager (association football)">manager</a> after a reported fee of €9.5&#160;million was agreed with PSV.<sup id="cite_ref-PN_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PN-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> He made his <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Serie_A" title="2013–14 Serie A">Serie A</a> debut on 25 August 2013, coming on as a second-half <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)" title="Substitute (association football)">substitute</a> for <a href="/wiki/Marek_Ham%C5%A1%C3%ADk" title="Marek Hamšík">Marek Hamšík</a> in a 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Bologna_F.C._1909" title="Bologna F.C. 1909">Bologna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> His first goal for Napoli came on 30 October when he netted the winner in a 2–1 away victory over <a href="/wiki/ACF_Fiorentina" title="ACF Fiorentina">Fiorentina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In Napoli's first game following the Serie A winter break on 6 January 2014, Mertens scored his first brace for the club in a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/U.C._Sampdoria" title="U.C. Sampdoria">Sampdoria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> He then scored Napoli's second goal in their 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> on 30 March, helping inflict only the second league defeat over the eventual champions.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2014_Coppa_Italia_Final" title="2014 Coppa Italia Final">final</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Coppa_Italia" title="2013–14 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> on 3 May 2014, Mertens replaced Marek Hamšík in the 64th minute and went on to score in stoppage time, securing a 3–1 win over Fiorentina.<sup id="cite_ref-CI1_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CI1-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mertens claimed another winners' medal on 22 December 2014 after Napoli's <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shoot-out</a> victory over Juventus in the <a href="/wiki/Supercoppa_Italiana" title="Supercoppa Italiana">Supercoppa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CI_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CI-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Despite being predominantly used as a substitute, he continued his fine form for Napoli over the course of the next season and a half, netting 10 goals and contributing 11 assists across all competitions in <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Serie_A" title="2014–15 Serie A">2014–15</a>, and 11 more goals in <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Serie_A" title="2015–16 Serie A">2015–16</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JH_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JH-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> His tally in the latter campaign included a brace in Napoli's joint-largest ever winning margin in the Europa League, a 5–0 win over Belgian side <a href="/wiki/Club_Brugge_KV" title="Club Brugge KV">Club Brugge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Mertens also scored a second-half hat-trick in a convincing 6–0 victory over Bologna on 19 April 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FC_Salzburg_versus_SSC_Napoli_(UEFA_Euroleague_Achtelfinalr%C3%BCckspiel_14._M%C3%A4rz_2019)_45.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/FC_Salzburg_versus_SSC_Napoli_%28UEFA_Euroleague_Achtelfinalr%C3%BCckspiel_14._M%C3%A4rz_2019%29_45.jpg/220px-FC_Salzburg_versus_SSC_Napoli_%28UEFA_Euroleague_Achtelfinalr%C3%BCckspiel_14._M%C3%A4rz_2019%29_45.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/FC_Salzburg_versus_SSC_Napoli_%28UEFA_Euroleague_Achtelfinalr%C3%BCckspiel_14._M%C3%A4rz_2019%29_45.jpg/330px-FC_Salzburg_versus_SSC_Napoli_%28UEFA_Euroleague_Achtelfinalr%C3%BCckspiel_14._M%C3%A4rz_2019%29_45.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/FC_Salzburg_versus_SSC_Napoli_%28UEFA_Euroleague_Achtelfinalr%C3%BCckspiel_14._M%C3%A4rz_2019%29_45.jpg/440px-FC_Salzburg_versus_SSC_Napoli_%28UEFA_Euroleague_Achtelfinalr%C3%BCckspiel_14._M%C3%A4rz_2019%29_45.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2586" data-file-height="2171" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FC_Salzburg_versus_SSC_Napoli_(UEFA_Euroleague_Achtelfinalr%C3%BCckspiel_14._M%C3%A4rz_2019)_45.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mertens (left) during Napoli's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> clash against <a href="/wiki/FC_Red_Bull_Salzburg" title="FC Red Bull Salzburg">Red Bull Salzburg</a> in 2019.</div></div></div>
<p>Following the sale of <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Higua%C3%ADn" title="Gonzalo Higuaín">Gonzalo Higuaín</a> – the previous season's <i><a href="/wiki/Capocannoniere" title="Capocannoniere">Capocannoniere</a></i> – to rivals Juventus, and a serious injury to his replacement <a href="/wiki/Arkadiusz_Milik" title="Arkadiusz Milik">Arkadiusz Milik</a>, Mertens assumed a more senior role in the centre of Napoli's attack for the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Serie_A" title="2016–17 Serie A">2016–17 Serie A season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Juventus_complete_Gonzalo_Higuain_signing_from_Napoli_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Juventus_complete_Gonzalo_Higuain_signing_from_Napoli-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JH_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JH-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> On 11 December 2016, he netted a hat-trick in a 5–0 Serie A victory over <a href="/wiki/Cagliari_Calcio" title="Cagliari Calcio">Cagliari</a> before taking it a step further in the next match by scoring four goals in a 5–3 win over <a href="/wiki/Torino_F.C." title="Torino F.C.">Torino</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Mertens' four goals, which included the fourth fastest hat-trick in Serie A history, was the first haul scored by a Napoli player since <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Savoldi" title="Giuseppe Savoldi">Beppe Savoldi</a> in 1977. It also saw him become the first player to score successive league hat-tricks since Juventus' <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Anastasi" title="Pietro Anastasi">Pietro Anastasi</a> in 1974, and the first to score seven goals across two matches since <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Angelillo" class="mw-redirect" title="Antonio Angelillo">Antonio Angelillo</a> in 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JH_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JH-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> His form for club and country was rewarded when, on 30 December, he was named Belgian Footballer of the Year for 2016, beating <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Eden_Hazard" title="Eden Hazard">Eden Hazard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radja_Nainggolan" title="Radja Nainggolan">Radja Nainggolan</a> of <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a> to the award.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BFOTY_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BFOTY-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 4 February 2017, Mertens and Hamšík both scored hat-tricks in a 7–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Bologna_F.C._1909" title="Bologna F.C. 1909">Bologna</a>, a result which saw Napoli score seven away goals in a match for the first time in the club's history.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> On the final day of the season he scored his 50th league goal for Napoli, and 28th for the campaign, ultimately ending one goal behind Golden Boot winner <a href="/wiki/Edin_D%C5%BEeko" title="Edin Džeko">Edin Džeko</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> He maintained his goal scoring form the following season during which he scored 22 goals for the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 28 November 2018, Mertens scored his 100th goal for Napoli when he netted twice in a 3–1 <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> win over <a href="/wiki/Red_Star_Belgrade" title="Red Star Belgrade">Red Star Belgrade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> He then made his 200th Serie A appearance for the club on 14 April 2019 in a 3–1 win over <a href="/wiki/A.C._ChievoVerona" title="A.C. ChievoVerona">Chievo</a>, marking the occasion with an assist for <a href="/wiki/Kalidou_Koulibaly" title="Kalidou Koulibaly">Kalidou Koulibaly</a>'s opening goal.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> On 28 April, Mertens scored in a 2–0 away win over <a href="/wiki/Frosinone_Calcio" title="Frosinone Calcio">Frosinone</a>, which allowed him to equal <a href="/wiki/Diego_Maradona" title="Diego Maradona">Diego Maradona</a>'s tally of 81 goals in Serie A for Napoli.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The following season, in October 2019, he surpassed Maradona's tally of 115 goals for the club across all competitions when he netted twice in a 3–2 <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2019–20 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> win over <a href="/wiki/FC_Red_Bull_Salzburg" title="FC Red Bull Salzburg">Red Bull Salzburg</a>, becoming the club's second-highest scorer of all time, behind Hamšík.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> On 25 February 2020, Mertens scored the opening goal in an eventual 1–1 home draw against <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> in the first leg of the round of 16 of the UEFA Champions League; with this goal, he tied Hamšík as Napoli's all-time highest goalscorer, with 121 goals. He was later substituted early in the second half due to injury.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> On 13 June, he scored the equalizing goal in a 1–1 home draw against <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a> in the second leg of <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Coppa_Italia" title="2019–20 Coppa Italia">2019–20 Coppa Italia</a> semi-final, which saw him overtake Hamšík to become Napoli's outright all-time leading goalscorer with 122 goals; the result also allowed Napoli to advanced to the <a href="/wiki/2020_Coppa_Italia_Final" title="2020 Coppa Italia Final">Coppa Italia Final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> On 17 June, he signed a two–year contract extension with the club. Later that day, he started in the Coppa Italia final against Juventus, and was later substituted for Milik in the second half; Napoli won 4–2 on penalties following a 0–0 draw after regulation time.<sup id="cite_ref-2020-CI_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020-CI-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dries_Mertens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth_career_and_early_senior_career">Youth career and early senior career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dries_Mertens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Youth career and early senior career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:178px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mertens_celebrating_bronze.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mertens_celebrating_bronze.jpg/176px-Mertens_celebrating_bronze.jpg" decoding="async" width="176" height="410" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mertens_celebrating_bronze.jpg/263px-Mertens_celebrating_bronze.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/28/Mertens_celebrating_bronze.jpg 2x" data-file-width="307" data-file-height="716" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mertens_celebrating_bronze.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mertens celebrating winning the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a> bronze medal following Belgium's 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> in the third place play-off.</div></div></div>
<p>Having previously represented Belgium at youth level, Mertens received his first senior call-up by <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">national team</a> coach <a href="/wiki/Georges_Leekens" title="Georges Leekens">Georges Leekens</a> on 1 October 2010 for the nation's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2012 qualifying">UEFA Euro 2012 qualifying matches</a> against <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan_national_football_team" title="Kazakhstan national football team">Kazakhstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austria_national_football_team" title="Austria national football team">Austria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Though he never featured in either match, Mertens would make his debut on 9 February the following year in a <a href="/wiki/Exhibition_game#association_football" title="Exhibition game">friendly</a> match against <a href="/wiki/Finland_national_football_team" title="Finland national football team">Finland</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jules_Ottenstadion" title="Jules Ottenstadion">Ghent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-f442_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-f442-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal for Belgium on 15 August 2012 in the 125th <i><a href="/wiki/Low_Countries_derby" title="Low Countries derby">Derby der Lage Landen</a></i>. Mertens, having come on as substitute for <a href="/wiki/Nacer_Chadli" title="Nacer Chadli">Nacer Chadli</a>, scored once and assisted twice, to help Belgium overcome a 2–1 deficit versus the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a> and win 4–2.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_FIFA_World_Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dries_Mertens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2014 FIFA World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mertens was named in <a href="/wiki/Marc_Wilmots" title="Marc Wilmots">Marc Wilmots</a>' 23-man squad for Belgium's <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a> campaign in Brazil on 13 May 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In the nation's final warm-up match for the tournament on 7 June, Mertens scored a late winner to secure a 1–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Tunisia_national_football_team" title="Tunisia national football team">Tunisia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> He made his first appearance in Belgium's opening match of the World Cup, replacing Chadli at half time and scoring a late winner in a 2–1 victory over <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria</a> in <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Prior to the World Cup, Mertens had made a bet with his father that he would score at the tournament. After the match, he posted a photo on <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> of him shaving his father's mustache off as reward for winning the bet.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> He made five appearances in total at the World Cup as Belgium were eliminated in the quarter-finals at the hands of eventual runners-up, <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UEFA_Euro_2016">UEFA Euro 2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dries_Mertens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: UEFA Euro 2016">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the World Cup, Belgium embarked on their <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_qualifying_Group_B" title="UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying Group B">qualification campaign</a> for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">Euro 2016</a>. Mertens netted his first brace for Belgium in their opening qualifying match, netting twice in three minutes in a 6–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Andorra_national_football_team" title="Andorra national football team">Andorra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The following year, he scored one and assisted another in a 3–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Israel_national_football_team" title="Israel national football team">Israel</a> which ensured that Belgium secured top spot in their qualifying group.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> He was later named in Belgium's squad for the tournament proper and featured in all five of the nation's matches as Belgium fell at the quarter-final stage once again, this time losing out to <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team" title="Wales national football team">Wales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_FIFA_World_Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dries_Mertens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2018 FIFA World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Under new manager <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Roberto Martínez">Roberto Martínez</a>, Mertens scored five goals in <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_I" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Group I">Belgium's qualification</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>, including two in an 8–1 home win over <a href="/wiki/Estonia_national_football_team" title="Estonia national football team">Estonia</a> on 13 November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> He was then selected in Belgium's tournament squad and scored in the nation's opening match in a 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Panama_national_football_team" title="Panama national football team">Panama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> He featured interchangeably as a starter and substitute for the remainder of the tournament as Belgium ended third, defeating <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_knockout_stage#Third_place_play-off" title="2018 FIFA World Cup knockout stage">third place play-off</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Belgium_secured_third_place_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belgium_secured_third_place-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dries_Mertens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A versatile and hard-working forward,<sup id="cite_ref-4-4-2_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4-4-2-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Mertens is a fast, creative, diminutive, and agile player, with a low centre of gravity, who possesses good technique and <a href="/wiki/Dribbling#Association_football" title="Dribbling">dribbling</a> skills, which enables him to get past opponents when in possession of the ball.<sup id="cite_ref-4-4-2_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4-4-2-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Possessing good vision, passing, shooting ability, movement off the ball, and an eye for goal, he is known for his ability both to score and <a href="/wiki/Assist_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Assist (football)">create</a> goals, and is capable of getting onto the end of passes or creating space for himself or his teammates by making attacking runs into the box.<sup id="cite_ref-4-4-2_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4-4-2-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gazza_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gazza-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> His favoured role is as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Winger" title="Forward (association football)">winger</a> on the left flank, a position which allows him to cut into the centre and strike on goal from outside the area with his stronger right foot,<sup id="cite_ref-4-4-2_69-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4-4-2-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> although he is also capable of playing on the right, and has even been used as an <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">attacking midfielder</a> by manager <a href="/wiki/Dick_Advocaat" title="Dick Advocaat">Dick Advocaat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4-4-2_69-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4-4-2-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gazza_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gazza-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> He is also an accurate <a href="/wiki/Direct_free_kick" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct free kick">free kick</a> taker.<sup id="cite_ref-4-4-2_69-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4-4-2-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> During the 2016–17 season, following the departure of Gonzalo Higuaín to rivals Juventus and an injury to the club's main striker Arkadiusz Milik, Napoli coach <a href="/wiki/Maurizio_Sarri" title="Maurizio Sarri">Maurizio Sarri</a> frequently deployed Dries Mertens either as a main striker, or in a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#False_9" title="Forward (association football)">false nine</a> role, seemingly positioned as a lone <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Centre-forward" title="Forward (association football)">centre-forward</a>, rather than as a left winger, where he had previously faced competition from <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Insigne" title="Lorenzo Insigne">Lorenzo Insigne</a> for a starting position; Sarri's tactical change was met with great results, and Mertens's goalscoring output increased dramatically as a result of this switch.<sup id="cite_ref-Juventus_complete_Gonzalo_Higuain_signing_from_Napoli_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Juventus_complete_Gonzalo_Higuain_signing_from_Napoli-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JH_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JH-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-self-sabotage_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-self-sabotage-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-divertirmi_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divertirmi-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<p><b>PSV</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/KNVB_Cup" title="KNVB Cup">KNVB Cup</a>: <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_KNVB_Cup" title="2011–12 KNVB Cup">2011–12</a><sup id="cite_ref-KNVB_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KNVB-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></li>

</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Coppa_Italia" title="Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a>: <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Coppa_Italia" title="2013–14 Coppa Italia">2013–14</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-CI1_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CI1-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Coppa_Italia" title="2019–20 Coppa Italia">2019–20</a><sup id="cite_ref-2020-CI_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020-CI-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li>
